Kernel: SageMath 9.5

In this notebook we compute the formal semigroups (as defined by S. Wang [Semigroups of L-space knots and nonalgebraic iterated torus knots]) of the SnapPy census L-space knots and check weather they are semigroups or not.

In [1]:
import snappy
In [2]:
def formal_semigroup(alex):
    '''Takes the Alexander polynomial of an L-space knot and returns its formal semigroup.'''
    for x in alex.coefficients():
        if abs(x)!=1:
            raise ValueError('The Alexander polynomial is not the polynomial of an L-space.')
    fsg=[]
    exp=alex.exponents()
    g=alex.degree()
    for i in range((len(exp)-1)/2):
        x=exp[2*i]
        y=exp[2*i+1]
        for j in range(g):
            if x+j<y:
                fsg.append(x+j)
    fsg.append(g)
    return [fsg,'+all values greater than',g]
In [3]:
def is_semigroup(fsg):
    '''Takes a formal semigroup and checks if it is a semi group.'''
    for x in fsg[0]:
        for y in fsg[0]:
            if x+y<=fsg[2]:
                if x+y not in fsg[0]:
                    return False # If x+y is not in fsg it is NOT a semigroup.
    return True # If this is the case it is a semigroup.

In [6]:
formal_semigroups=[]
for name in L_space_knots:
    K=snappy.Manifold(name)
    alex=K.alexander_polynomial()
    fsg=formal_semigroup(alex)
    formal_semigroups.append([name,is_semigroup(fsg),fsg])
In [7]:
formal_semigroups

Out[8]:
['t09847', True, [[0, 4, 7, 8, 10, 11, 12, 14], '+all values greater than', 14]] ['o9_30634', True, [[0, 4, 6, 8, 9, 10, 12], '+all values greater than', 12]]

We have shown that o9_30634 and t09847 are the only census L-space knots whose formal semigroup is a semigroup. In particular, both are negative answers to Question 2.8 in Wang's paper. It is known that any algebraic knot is an L-space knot whose formal semigroup is a semigroup. On the other hand, algebraic knots are known to be iterated cables of torus knots and are therefore not hyperbolic. Question 2.8 in Wang's paper asks if there exists an L-space knot which is not an iterated torus knot whose formal semigroup is a semigroup. Since our examples are hyperbolic they cannot be iterated torus knots and thus negatively answers Wang's question. Actually, both knots fit into an infinite family of hyperbolic L-space knots whose formal semigroups are semigroups.

We work with the infinite family that corresponds to o9_30634. The other family can be studied in exactly the same way.

In [9]:
for n in range(1,30):
    word=(2*n+1)*[2,1,3,2]+[-1,2,1,1,2] # n=1 yields the knot 09_30634.
    D=snappy.Link(braid_closure=word)
    K=D.exterior()
    alex=K.alexander_polynomial()
    fsg=formal_semigroup(alex)
    print(2*n+1,is_semigroup(fsg),fsg)
